## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Population Ecology / Mathematical Biology
**Analysis**: The task models the instantaneous rate of change of a population (dP/dt) as a function of its current size (P) and time (t), which is a foundational problem in population ecology and mathematical biology. The underlying relationships typically involve density-dependent regulation, environmental modulation, or harvesting pressures that shape growth trajectories.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent population increase)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - c2 * P) (density-dependent regulation approaching carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * log(P)) (sigmoidal dynamics with logarithmic density dependence)
- Theta-logistic rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - c2 * P**c3) (flexible non-linear density feedback)
- Allee effect rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - c2) * (c3 - c4 * P) (growth suppression at low and high densities)
- Ricker-type continuous rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (strong overcompensatory density dependence)
- Seasonal environmental modulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) (periodic environmental drivers affecting growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous rate: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * P) (smooth saturation of per-capita growth)
- Time-varying capacity model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * t - c3 * P) (linearly shifting environmental carrying capacity)
- Harvesting/Schaefer model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - c2 * P) - c3 * P (logistic dynamics with constant proportional extraction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Intraspecific competition feedback → Quadratic mortality term c0*P - c1*P**2 or cubic interaction c0*P - c1*P**3
- Allee effect / critical density → Bimodal sign change in growth rate via product terms (c0*P-c1)*(c2-c3*P)
- Overcompensatory regulation → Exponential decay of per-capita rate with population size exp(c*P) where c<0
- Sigmoidal population trajectory → Logarithmic density dependence c*P*log(P) producing asymmetric S-curves
- Environmental seasonality → Harmonic modulation of intrinsic rate c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3)
- Habitat carrying capacity drift → Time-linear addition within density bracket (c0 + c1*t - c2*P)
- Proportional harvesting/exploitation → Linear subtraction term -c*P representing constant mortality pressure

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`GT = c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4/(c5*P + c6)`
Substituting the given numerical constants (`c4=2.0`), we get:
`GT = A*P - B*P**2 + C*P**2/(D*P + 1)`
where `A, B, C, D` are fixed non-zero constants. Combining over a common denominator `(D*P + 1)`:
`GT = [ (A*P - B*P**2)*(D*P + 1) + C*P**2 ] / (D*P + 1)`
`GT = [ -B*D*P**3 + (A*D - B + C)*P**2 + A*P ] / (D*P + 1)`
Factoring out `P` from the numerator:
`GT = P * ( a*P**2 + b*P + c ) / ( d*P + 1 )`
where `a, b, c, d` are constants derived from the GT parameters. Crucially, the coefficient `b` (for the linear `P` term inside the quadratic) is non-zero (`≈ 7.836`). ## Ground Truth Analysis

GT: `0.9198*(1 - P/84.028)*P + 0.9198*P²/(7.531*P + 1)`

Let me expand:
= 0.9198*P - 0.9198*P²/84.028 + 0.9198*P²/(7.531*P + 1)
= 0.9198*P - 0.01095*P² + 0.9198*P²/(7.531*P + 1)

Let me combine over common denominator (7.531*P + 1):
= [0.9198*P*(7.531*P + 1) - 0.01095*P²*(7.531*P + 1) + 0.9198*P²] / (7.531*P + 1)

Numerator:
= 6.927*P² + 0.9198*P - 0.08243*P³ - 0.01095*P² + 0.9198*P²
= -0.08243*P³ + (6.927 - 0.01095 + 0.9198)*P² + 0.9198*P
= -0.08243*P³ + 7.836*P² + 0.9198*P

So GT = P*(-0.08243*P² + 7.836*P + 0.9198) / (7.531*P + 1)

This is: **P*(aP² + bP + c) / (dP + 1)** where a < 0, b > 0, c > 0, d > 0.

Equivalently: **P*(c0*P² + c1*P + c2) / (c3*P + 1)**

Now let me check candidates systematically.

### Candidate 1: P*(c0*(P + c1) + (P*c2 + c3)*(P²*c4 + c5))/((P + c1)*(P*c2 + c3))

Simplify: P*[c0/(P*c2+c3) + (P²*c4+c5)/(P+c1)] — wait, let me be more careful.

= P*[c0*(P+c1) + (P*c2+c3)*(P²*c4+c5)] / [(P+c1)*(P*c2+c3)]

The second term simplifies to P*(P²*c4+c5)/(P+c1) + P*c0/(P*c2+c3)

This has the form: P*f(P)/(P+c1) + P*g(P)/(P*c2+c3)

GT has the form: P*linear(P) + P²/(linear(P))

The first part of GT: c0*(1-P/c2)*P = aP + bP² — a polynomial in P.
The second part: c3*P²/(c5*P+c6) — rational.

So GT = polynomial(P) + P²/(linear(P)).

For Candidate 1, we get two rational terms with different denominators. Can this match GT?

We need: P*c0/(P*c2+c3) to be a polynomial. That requires c2=0, giving constant c0/c3. Then the other term is P*(P²*c4+c5)/(P+c1). 

GT = aP + bP² + dP²/(eP+1). Over denominator (eP+1): [aP(eP+1) + bP²(eP+1) + dP²]/(eP+1) = [beP³ + (ae+b+d)P² + aP]/(eP+1).

With c2=0: Candidate 1 = P*c0/c3 + P*(P²*c4+c5)/(P+c1) = P*A + P*(c4*P²+c5)/(P+c1)

Over (P+c1): [A*P*(P+c1) + P*(c4*P²+c5)]/(P+c1) = P*[c4*P² + A*P + (A*c1+c5)]/(P+c1)

This is P*(cubic-becomes-quadratic? No, it's P*(c4*P²+AP+(Ac1+c5)))/(P+c1) = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c1).

GT = P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). Setting c1 = 1/d, this matches! Yes.

Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 2: P*(c0*(P + c1) + (P*c2 + 1)*(P²*c3 + c4))/((P + c1)*(P*c2 + 1))

= P*c0/(P*c2+1) + P*(P²*c3+c4)/(P+c1)

Full numerator (times P): P*(c2*c3*P³ + c3*P² + (c0+c2*c4)*P + (c0*c1+c4))

Denominator: (P+c1)*(c2*P+1) = c2*P² + (1+c1*c2)*P + c1

GT = P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). The denominator is linear in P, but here it's quadratic. To make it linear, set c1=0: denominator = P*(c2*P+1), and numerator becomes P*(c2*c3*P³+c3*P²+(c0+c2*c4)*P+c4).

If c3=0: (c0+c2*c4)*P+c4)/(c2*P+1) — that's degree 1/degree 1, giving us P*(linear)/(linear), which is only degree 2 rational, not matching GT's degree 3 numerator.

If c2=0: denominator = (P+c1)*1 = P+c1, numerator = P*(c3*P²+(c0+c4)P+c0*c1+c4) — wait, let me redo with c2=0:

So: P*(c3*P²+c0*P+(c0*c1+c4))/(P+c1) = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c1)

This matches GT form! Yes.

### Candidate 3: (c0*(P+1) + (P*c1+1)*(P³*c2+P²*c3+P*c4+c5))/((P+1)*(P*c1+1))

= c0/(P*c1+1) + (P³*c2+P²*c3+P*c4+c5)/(P+1)

GT has no constant term (GT=0 when P=0). At P=0: c0/1 + c5/1 = c0+c5. Set c0+c5=0, so c5=-c0.

Then: c0/(c1*P+1) + (c2*P³+c3*P²+c4*P-c0)/(P+1)

For this to match GT = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(δP+1), we need specific structure. The two different denominators (c1*P+1) and (P+1) make this complicated. If c1=1: both denominators are (P+1), and we get [c0+c2*P³+c3*P²+c4*P-c0]/(P+1) = (c2*P³+c3*P²+c4*P)/(P+1) = P*(c2*P²+c3*P+c4)/(P+1). This matches GT form with δ=1. But GT has δ=7.531, so P+1 vs 7.531P+1. We can't freely choose the denominator coefficient independently since c1 is already set to 1 to merge denominators.

Wait — if c1≠1, we have two different denominators. Let me try c1 = 7.531. Then denominator is (P+1)*(7.531P+1).

Numerator: c0*(P+1) + (7.531P+1)*(c2*P³+c3*P²+c4*P+c5)

For GT over this denominator: GT = P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)/(7.531P+1)/(P+1) — wait, GT = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(7.531P+1).

Over (P+1)*(7.531P+1): P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)/(7.531P+1)/(P+1) — no.

GT*(P+1)*(7.531P+1) = P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)

This is a degree 4 polynomial in P.

Candidate 3 numerator: c0*(P+1) + (7.531P+1)*(c2*P³+c3*P²+c4*P+c5)

The (7.531P+1)*(c2*P³+...) term gives degree 4 polynomial. And c0*(P+1) is degree 1. Total: degree 4 polynomial with 6 free constants (c0,c2,c3,c4,c5 — 5 constants). GT*(P+1)*(7.531P+1) is degree 4 with 4 coefficients (P⁴,P³,P²,P, and constant=0). So 5 equations, 5 unknowns. This should work if the system is consistent.

GT*denominator = P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1) = P*(αP³+(α+β)P²+(β+γ)P+γ) = αP⁴+(α+β)P³+(β+γ)P²+γP

Candidate numerator with c1=7.531:
= c0*P+c0 + 7.531c2*P⁴+(7.531c3+c2)P³+(7.531c4+c3)P²+(7.531c5+c4)P+c5

Matching coefficients:
- P⁴: 7.531*c2 = α → c2 = α/7.531
- P³: 7.531*c3+c2 = α+β → c3 = (α+β-c2)/7.531
- P²: 7.531*c4+c3 = β+γ → c4 = (β+γ-c3)/7.531
- P¹: 7.531*c5+c4+c0 = γ
- P⁰: c5+c0 = 0 → c5 = -c0

From P¹: 7.531*(-c0)+c4+c0 = γ → c4-6.531*c0 = γ → c0 = (c4-γ)/6.531

This system has 5 equations and 5 unknowns (c0,c2,c3,c4,c5), which is determined. It should have a solution.

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4: P*(P²*c0 + P*c1*(P+c2) + c3)/(P+c2)

= P*(c0*P² + c1*P² + c1*c2*P + c3)/(P+c2)
= P*((c0+c1)*P² + c1*c2*P + c3)/(P+c2)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c2), which is a cubic numerator over linear denominator times P. But GT is P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). Here the constraint is β = c1*c2 and α = c0+c1, γ = c3, denominator shift = c2. But α, β, γ, c2 are determined by 4 GT parameters, and we have c0, c1, c2, c3 — 4 free parameters. 

However, there's a constraint: β/(denominator constant) = c1*c2/c2 = c1, and α-c1 = c0. So β = c1*c2 is free (c1 and c2 are free). Actually, α = c0+c1, β = c1*c2, γ = c3, denominator = P+c2. We need to match P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). Setting c2 = 1/d, we need α = a, β = b, γ = c. We have 4 unknowns (c0,c1,c2,c3) and 4 equations: c2=1/d, c0+c1=a, c1*c2=b, c3=c. From c2=1/d and c1=b/c2=b*d, c0=a-b*d. All determined. This works!

Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 5: (P*(P²*c0+c1) + c2*(P+c3)*|P|²)/(P+c3)

For P≥0, |P|²=P². So:
= (P³*c0+P*c1+c2*P²*(P+c3))/(P+c3)
= (P³*c0+P*c1+c2*P³+c2*c3*P²)/(P+c3)
= ((c0+c2)*P³+c2*c3*P²+c1*P)/(P+c3)
= P*((c0+c2)*P²+c2*c3*P+c1)/(P+c3)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c3) with constraint β=c2*c3 and α=c0+c2. We have 4 free params (c0,c1,c2,c3) and need to match 4 GT params. Same as Candidate 4 analysis. Works!

Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 6: P*(P²*c0+c1+c2*(P+c3)*Max(0,P+c4))/(P+c3)

For P≥0, if c4≥0, Max(0,P+c4)=P+c4. If c4<0, it's piecewise. Let me try c4 large enough that P+c4>0 for all relevant P. Then Max(0,P+c4)=P+c4.

= P*(c0*P²+c1+c2*(P+c3)*(P+c4))/(P+c3)
= P*(c0*P²+c1)/(P+c3) + P*c2*(P+c4)

= P*c2*(P+c4) + P*(c0*P²+c1)/(P+c3)

The first part is a polynomial c2*P²+c2*c4*P. The second is P*(c0*P²+c1)/(P+c3).

Over common denominator: P*[c2*(P+c4)*(P+c3)+c0*P²+c1]/(P+c3)
= P*[c2*P²+(c2*c4+c2*c3)*P+c2*c3*c4+c0*P²+c1]/(P+c3)
= P*[(c0+c2)*P²+(c2*c4+c2*c3)*P+(c2*c3*c4+c1)]/(P+c3)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c3) with enough free parameters. But the issue is Max(0, P+c4) — this is only valid when P+c4≥0. If we set c4=0, Max(0,P)=P for P≥0, and we get:

P*(c0*P²+c1+c2*(P+c3)*P)/(P+c3) = P*(c0*P²+c1+c2*P²+c2*c3*P)/(P+c3) = P*((c0+c2)*P²+c2*c3*P+c1)/(P+c3)

Same form. But the Max function makes this not a smooth algebraic expression in general. However, for P≥0 with appropriate c4, it works. Given domain constraints (P≥0), setting c4=0 makes Max(0,P)=P, giving the right form.

Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 7: (P*c0*(P*c1+1)+P*c2+c3*(P*c1+1)+c4*(P*c1+1)*|P|²+c5)/(P*c1+1)

For P≥0, |P|²=P².

= P*c0 + P*c2/(P*c1+1) + c3 + c4*P² + c5/(P*c1+1)

= c4*P² + c0*P + c3 + (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1)

GT = aP + bP² + dP²/(eP+1) = bP² + aP + dP²/(eP+1)

For this to match, we need (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1) = dP²/(eP+1). But the left side is degree 1/degree 1 (approaches c2/c1 as P→∞), while dP²/(eP+1) approaches dP/e as P→∞. These have different asymptotic behavior. So they can't be equal.

Unless c4*P² absorbs part of it... Let me reconsider.

GT = bP² + aP + dP²/(eP+1). Let me write this as (b + d/(eP+1))*P² + aP.

Candidate 7 = c4*P² + c0*P + c3 + (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1)

Setting c3=0: c4*P² + c0*P + (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1)

We need c4*P² + c0*P + (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1) = bP² + aP + dP²/(eP+1)

So (c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1) = (b-c4)*P² + (a-c0)*P + dP²/(eP+1)

The left side is O(1) as P→∞, but the right side is O(P) unless b=c4 and a=c0. If b=c4 and a=c0:

(c2*P+c5)/(c1*P+1) = dP²/(eP+1)

Left is degree 0 for large P, right is degree 1. Not equal. No match.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 8: (P*(P*c0+c1)*(P*c2+1)+c3*(P*c2+1)*Max(0,P+c4)+c5)/(P*c2+1)

= P*(c0*P+c1) + c3*Max(0,P+c4) + c5/(P*c2+1)

For P≥0 with c4≥0: Max(0,P+c4)=P+c4.

= c0*P²+c1*P+c3*P+c3*c4+c5/(c2*P+1)

= c0*P²+(c1+c3)*P+c3*c4+c5/(c2*P+1)

GT = bP²+aP+dP²/(eP+1). The last term of candidate is c5/(c2*P+1) which is O(1/P), while GT's last term dP²/(eP+1) is O(P). Not matchable.

Unless we use c5=0: then c0*P²+(c1+c3)*P+c3*c4. This is a polynomial, but GT has a rational part. No match.

Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 9: (c0+(P*c1+1)*(P²*c2+P*c3+c4))/(P*c1+1)

= c0/(P*c1+1) + P²*c2+P*c3+c4

GT = bP²+aP+dP²/(eP+1). We need c0/(c1*P+1) = dP²/(eP+1) — impossible (degree 0 vs degree 1 for large P). Unless we absorb differently:

c2*P²+c3*P+c4+c0/(c1*P+1) vs bP²+aP+dP²/(eP+1)

Setting c2=b, c3=a, c4=0: c0/(c1*P+1) = dP²/(eP+1). Left is O(1/P), right is O(P). No match.

Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 10: (P*c0+c1+(P*c2+c3)*(P²*c4+P*c5+c6))/(P*c2+c3)

= (P*c0+c1)/(P*c2+c3) + P²*c4+P*c5+c6

= c4*P²+c5*P+c6 + (c0*P+c1)/(c2*P+c3)

GT = bP²+aP + dP²/(eP+1). We need (c0*P+c1)/(c2*P+c3) = dP²/(eP+1) + (terms absorbed into polynomial).

Setting c4=b, c5=a, c6=0: (c0*P+c1)/(c2*P+c3) = dP²/(eP+1). Same issue — left is O(1), right is O(P). No match.

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 11: P*(c0*(P+1)+(P*c1+c2)*(P²*c3+P*c4+c5))/((P+1)*(P*c1+c2))

= P*[c0/(P*c1+c2) + (P²*c3+P*c4+c5)/(P+1)]

If c2=c1 (so P*c1+c2=c1*(P+1)): = P*[c0/(c1*(P+1)) + (c3*P²+c4*P+c5)/(P+1)] = P*(c0/c1+c3*P²+c4*P+c5)/(P+1) = P*(c3*P²+c4*P+(c5+c0/c1))/(P+1)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+1), matching GT form with denominator P+1. But GT denominator is 7.531P+1, i.e., P+1/7.531. We can't get P+c with c≠1 from (P+1). So this doesn't work with c2=c1.

Let me try differently. With general c1,c2:

= P*c0/(P*c1+c2) + P*(c3*P²+c4*P+c5)/(P+1)

Two different denominators. Over (P+1)*(c1*P+c2):

P*[c0*(P+1) + (c1*P+c2)*(c3*P²+c4*P+c5)] / [(P+1)*(c1*P+c2)]

Numerator: P*[c0*P+c0 + c1*c3*P³+c1*c4*P²+c1*c5*P+c2*c3*P²+c2*c4*P+c2*c5]
= P*[c1*c3*P³+(c1*c4+c2*c3)P²+(c0+c1*c5+c2*c4)P+(c0+c2*c5)]

Denominator: (P+1)*(c1*P+c2) = c1*P²+(c1+c2)*P+c2

GT = P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). GT over (P+1)*(dP+1) would be P*(aP²+bP+c)*(P+1)/[(dP+1)*(P+1)].

For candidate to match GT, we need the candidate's denominator to factor appropriately. If c1*P+c2 = c1*(P+c2/c1). We need (P+1)*(c1*P+c2) to relate to (dP+1) somehow. This requires (P+1) to cancel from numerator and denominator.

For (P+1) to cancel from numerator, we need P=-1 to be a root of the numerator polynomial. The inner polynomial at P=-1: c1*c3*(-1)³+(c1*c4+c2*c3)-( c0+c1*c5+c2*c4)+c0+c2*c5 = -c1*c3+c1*c4+c2*c3-c0-c1*c5-c2*c4+c0+c2*c5 = c1*(c4-c3-c5)+c2*(c3-c4+c5).

This can be set to 0 by choosing constants appropriately. Then after cancellation, we'd have P*(cubic)/(c1*P+c2), which could give P*(quadratic)/(linear) = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(c1*P+c2). This matches GT form!

So yes, with appropriate constants, this works.

Candidate 11 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 12: P*(P*c0*(P*c1+1)+P*c1+c2+c3*(P*c1+1))/(P*c1+1)

= P*[c0*P + (P*c1+c2)/(P*c1+1) + c3]

Wait, let me expand:
= P*[c0*P*(c1*P+1) + c1*P + c2 + c3*(c1*P+1)] / (c1*P+1)
= P*[c0*c1*P² + c0*P + c1*P + c2 + c3*c1*P + c3] / (c1*P+1)
= P*[c0*c1*P² + (c0+c1+c3*c1)*P + (c2+c3)] / (c1*P+1)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(c1*P+1), matching GT form!

Candidate 12 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 13: P*(P²*c0+P*c1+c2)/(P+c3)

This is directly P*(c0*P²+c1*P+c2)/(P+c3). GT = P*(aP²+bP+c)/(dP+1). Setting c3=1/d, c0=a, c1=b, c2=c. Perfect match!

Candidate 13 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 14: P*(P²*c0+P*c1+c2)/(P*c3+1)

Same as GT form directly: P*(c0*P²+c1*P+c2)/(c3*P+1). 

Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 15: P*(P²*c0+c1+c2*(P+c3))/(P+c3)

= P*(c0*P²+c2*P+c2*c3+c1)/(P+c3)
= P*(c0*P²+c2*P+(c1+c2*c3))/(P+c3)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c3) with constraint that β and the denominator constant are linked through c2 and c3. We have 4 free params (c0,c1,c2,c3) and need to match 4 GT params (a,b,c,d where d=1/c3). So c3=1/d, c0=a, c2=b, c1=c-b/d. This works!

Candidate 15 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 16: P*(c0+(P+c1)*(P*c2+c3))/(P+c1)

Over (P+c1): P*[(c2*P+c3)*(P+c1)+c0]/(P+c1) = P*[c2*P²+(c2*c1+c3)*P+c3*c1+c0]/(P+c1)

This is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c1). Matches GT form with 4 free params.

P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(P+c1). 4 free params, matches GT form.

Candidate 17 verdict: [MATCH]

Expanding c0*(P+c1)*(c2*P+c3) = c0*[c2*P²+(c3+c1*c2)*P+c1*c3]

So: P*[c0*c2*P²+c0*(c3+c1*c2)*P+c0*c1*c3+c4]/(c2*P+c3)

### Candidate 48: ((P+1)*(P*c0+c1)+(P*c2+c3)*(P³*c4+P²*c5+P*c6+c7))/((P+1)*(P*c2+c3))

= (P*c0+c1)/(P*c2+c3) + (P³*c4+P²*c5+P*c6+c7)/(P+1)

Two rational terms with different denominators. If c2=0: (c0*P+c1)/c3 + (c4*P³+c5*P²+c6*P+c7)/(P+1). The first is linear, second is cubic/linear. Combined over (P+1): [(c0*P+c1)(P+1)/c3 + c4*P³+c5*P²+c6*P+c7]/(P+1). This gives degree 3 numerator / (P+1). But GT is P*(degree 2)/(linear). If the degree 3 numerator has P as factor and (P+1) denominator... this could work but the denominator is fixed at (P+1), while GT needs (dP+1) with d=7.531.

Let me try with general c2,c3. Setting c3=c2 so P*c2+c3=c2*(P+1): then everything has denominator (P+1)²... no, denominator is (P+1)*(c2*(P+1)) = c2*(P+1)².

Hmm, let me try differently. Can we cancel (P+1) from numerator and denominator?

Actually, let me reconsider. The full expression is:

[(P+1)*(c0*P+c1) + (c2*P+c3)*(c4*P³+c5*P²+c6*P+c7)] / [(P+1)*(c2*P+c3)]

The numerator is degree 4 (from the second product), denominator is degree 2. So the result is degree 2 + proper fraction. GT is P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(δP+1), which for large P behaves as ~αP²/δ, i.e., degree 1. But degree 4/degree 2 behaves as degree 2. So we'd need the leading coefficient of the degree 4 numerator to be zero, making it effectively degree 3 / degree 2, which is degree 1 + proper fraction. That could work.

Let me set c4=0 to reduce degree: numerator becomes (P+1)*(c0*P+c1) + (c2*P+c3)*(c5*P²+c6*P+c7), which is degree 3. Denominator is degree 2. Result is degree 1 + proper fraction.

GT = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(δP+1). Over (P+1)*(δP+1): P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1) / [(P+1)*(δP+1)] — wait, GT denominator is just (δP+1), not (P+1)*(δP+1).

For the candidate to equal GT, we need:
[(P+1)*(c0*P+c1) + (c2*P+c3)*(c5*P²+c6*P+c7)] / [(P+1)*(c2*P+c3)] = P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(δP+1)

This means: numerator = P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)*(c2*P+c3) / (δP+1)

For this to be a polynomial, (δP+1) must divide (P+1)*(c2*P+c3). If c2*P+c3 = c2*(P+1/(δ*... )) — this gets complicated. Let me try c2*P+c3 = c2/δ*(δP+1), i.e., c3=c2/δ. Then (c2*P+c3) = c2*(P+1/δ) = (c2/δ)*(δP+1).

Then denominator = (P+1)*(c2/δ)*(δP+1), and GT*denominator = P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)*(c2/δ).

Numerator: (P+1)*(c0*P+c1) + (c2/δ)*(δP+1)*(c5*P²+c6*P+c7)

We need this to equal P*(αP²+βP+γ)*(P+1)*(c2/δ).

Hmm, this is getting complex but in principle with enough free parameters (c0,c1,c5,c6,c7 — 5 params) and 4 equations (coefficients of P³,P²,P,P⁰ in the degree 3 polynomial, plus the constraint that P=0 gives 0), it should be solvable.

At P=0: (1)*(c1) + (c2/δ)*(1)*(c7) = 0 → c1 + c2*c7/δ = 0.

This system should have solutions. So yes, this can match.

Candidate 48 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 50: (P²*c0*(P+1)+P*(P³*c1+P²*c2+P*c3+c4)+c5*(P+1))/(P*(P+1))

= P*c0 + (P³*c1+P²*c2+P*c3+c4)/(P+1) + c5/P

Has 1/P term. For P>0, GT doesn't have a 1/P singularity (GT(0)=0 smoothly). Setting c5=0:

= P*c0 + (c1*P³+c2*P²+c3*P+c4)/(P+1)

= [c0*P*(P+1) + c1*P³+c2*P²+c3*P+c4]/(P+1)
= [(c0+c1)*P³+(c0+c2)*P²+c3*P+c4]/(P+1) — wait, c0*P*(P+1) = c0*P²+c0*P.

= [c1*P³+(c0+c2)*P²+(c0+c3)*P+c4]/(P+1)

For GT: P*(αP²+βP+γ)/(δP+1). With denominator (P+1), δ=1. But GT has δ=7.531. The denominator is fixed at (P+1), can't match (7.531P+1).

Unless... we need c4=0 for GT(0)=0. Then numerator = P*[c1*P²+(c0+c2)*P+(c0+c3)]/(P+1). This is P*(quadratic)/(P+1), matching GT form only if δ=1. But GT has δ=7.531. No match.

Candidate 50 verdict: [NO MATCH]
